Top 3 returned. I want to refine the scoring philosophy of the app based on actual gameplay strategy. Keep the existing architecture intact. Important strategic principles: 1. Do not over-reward early “commitment.” The system should prefer focused flexibility, not rigid lock-in. A strong recommendation should represent the best lane right now while still allowing plausible pivots. 2. Do not reward scattered pairs just because they exist. Pairs are only valuable when they support a strong, viable hand path. Random pairs should not inflate a hand’s ranking. 3. Discount honor pairs unless they clearly fit the hand. Winds and dragons should not be treated as inherently valuable unless the hand specifically wants them and the rest of the structure supports that direction. 4. Joker value must be contextual. Jokers should help more when they support an already viable hand, especially in claimable groups. They should not give a large flat bonus to weak or overly rigid hands. 5. Add stronger penalties for “too dependent on luck” hands. Specifically, hands that require too many exact natural tiles, missing pairs, or rare/specific tiles should be penalized more heavily. 6. Reward path clarity. Hands should score better when: * the player already has meaningful support toward them * the missing pieces are clear * jokers can realistically help fill the gaps 7. Favor path viability over visible progress. A hand that is numerically closer but rigid or exact should often rank below a hand that is slightly less complete but more flexible and realistic to finish. Please update the scoring logic to reflect these principles without changing the app structure or output format. Now inline into the app: Ran a command, read a file Ran a command, read a file Here's what changed and why for each principle: Principle 1 — No over-rewarding rigidity: Added a rigidityPenalty — each single group beyond 2 in a hand adds a penalty. Hands with 4+ single positions are inherently inflexible (exact tiles, no joker, no claiming) and now score lower for it. Principle 2 — Scattered pairs don't inflate: Added scatteredPairPenalty — if a hand's matched tiles are mostly pairs with zero claimable structure behind them, the score is reduced. Pairs only count when they sit inside a real hand path. Principle 3 — Honor pairs discounted: Wind and dragon groups in pair/single positions are now weighted at 70% of normal in non-Winds & Dragons hands. An isolated North Wind pair doesn't help you in a 369 hand and shouldn't make it score higher. Principle 4 — Contextual joker bonus: Joker now gives 7 points per joker when the hand is viable (fitScore ≥ 35), but only 3 points on weak hands. A joker propping up a scattered hand doesn't get full credit. Principle 5 — Steeper must-draw compounding: The compound penalty curve is steeper — 0 tiles=0, 1=3pts, 2=10pts, 3=21pts. Hands requiring 3+ natural draws are significantly discounted now. Principle 6 & 7 — Path clarity rewarded: readyToCall groups get a stronger claim bonus (0.55 vs 0.50). readyWithJoker gets meaningful but not equal relief (0.35). pullMoreThenCall gets a small bonus (0.10) — it's claimable eventually, just not now. Overall penalty multiplier raised slightly to 2.2 to make the gap between clear and unclear paths more meaningful. This is exactly right. Where New Scoring May Over-Penalize Scattered pair penalty is too binary. It fires whenever ≥2 pairs matched and 0 claimable — but some legitimate hands have a pair-heavy early structure before claimable groups develop. A player holding pair of 2s and pair of 6s toward a 2468 hand is not "scattered" — those pairs are on-path. The condition matchedClaimable === 0 is too strict. It should check whether the matched pairs are on-path for the hand being scored, not just whether claimable tiles happened to fire first. Rigidity penalty may double-count with pairSingleMult. Singles already get penalized harder via pairSingleMult: 1.5 in the per-group penalty. Then rigidity adds another flat 4pts per extra single at the hand level. A hand with 4 singles takes (4-2)×4 = 8pts rigidity penalty ON TOP of elevated per-group penalties. For hands that score in the 30-50 range this could be decisive. Sensitivity Ranking — Most to Least Likely to Need Tuning 1. Scattered pair penalty (matchedPairCount × 3 / matchedClaimable === 0) Most sensitive and most likely wrong. The condition is too blunt — it doesn't distinguish between on-path pairs and genuinely random pairs. Needs to be hand-context aware or use a softer threshold. 2. Joker bonus threshold (fitScore ≥ 35) 35 is a reasonable line but arbitrary. A hand at fitScore 34 vs 36 gets very different joker treatment (3pts vs 7pts per joker = 4-8pt swing with 1-2 jokers). Could create cliff effects right at the boundary. Consider a gradient instead of a hard threshold. 3. Final penalty multiplier (2.2) Amplifies everything. A 0.1 change here ripples across every scored hand. Currently 2.2 vs old 2.0 — the 10% increase affects all penalties proportionally. Most impactful single constant in the formula. 4. Compound penalty curve The jump from 1 must-draw tile (3pts) to 2 (12pts) is large. That's a 9pt swing for one additional required natural draw. May suppress valid hands that need 2 pairs completed but are otherwise strong. 5. Claim bonuses (0.55 / 0.35 / 0.10) Reasonable spacing but readyWithJoker at 0.35 may be slightly high — placing a joker is a real commitment that reduces future flexibility. 0.25-0.30 may be more accurate. 6. Honor discount (0.7) Conservative and directionally correct. Could go to 0.5 for more aggressive suppression of honor noise. Unlikely to cause over-penalization since it only fires on non-WD hands. 7. Rigidity penalty ((singleCount-2) × 4) Least sensitive only because few hands have 3+ singles. When it does fire it's significant, but most hands won't trigger it. Keep the current architecture exactly as is. Modified scoreGroup (changes only — rest unchanged) javascript function scoreGroup(g, suit, pool) { let holds = 0; // ... [tile counting logic unchanged] ... const effective = Math.min(holds, g.count); const stillNeeded = Math.max(0, g.count - effective); // ... [pool consumption unchanged] ... // ... [weight calculation unchanged] ... const canClaim = g.groupType!=='single' && g.groupType!=='pair'; const claimBonus = canClaim ? 0.4 : 0; // NEW: differentiate pair completion difficulty by how many tiles held // replaces flat pairSingleMult let pairSingleMult = 1.0; if (!canClaim && stillNeeded > 0) { if (g.groupType === 'pair') { if (holds === 1) pairSingleMult = 1.3; // partial pair — one held, one needed if (holds === 0) pairSingleMult = 1.8; // missing pair — need both tiles naturally } else if (g.groupType === 'single') { pairSingleMult = 1.4; // singles still harder than claimable, same as before } } const penalty = stillNeeded * weight * (1 - claimBonus) * pairSingleMult; // ... [dragonNote logic unchanged] ... return { effective, stillNeeded, penalty, canClaim, dragonNote, holds, groupIsClaimable: canClaim }; } Modified scoreHand (changes only — structure unchanged) javascript function scoreHand(handDef, suitMap, hand) { // ... [pool, sort, loop, claiming state all unchanged] ... // ── Per-group penalty (inside loop) ───────────────────────────── // honor discount: unchanged at 0.7 for non-WD honor pairs/singles // claim bonus: unchanged // const claimBonus = readyToCall:0.55 / readyWithJoker:0.35 / pullMoreThenCall:0.10 / 0 // pairSingleMult: now comes from scoreGroup return value // scoreGroup now returns pairSingleMult baked into its penalty // groupPenalty = r.stillNeeded * w * (1-claimBonus) * r.pairSingleMult // [NOTE: pairSingleMult moved INTO scoreGroup — no change to groupPenalty formula structure] // ── After loop ─────────────────────────────────────────────────── const fitScore = Math.round((matched/total)*100); // 1. JOKER BONUS — gradient replaces hard threshold // OLD: jokers * (fitScore>=35 ? 7 : 3) // NEW: smooth linear scale from 3 (fit=0) to 8 (fit=100) const jokerViabilityScale = 3 + (fitScore / 100) * 5; // 3.0 at fit=0, 8.0 at fit=100 const jokerBonus = hand.jokers * jokerViabilityScale; // 2. CALL BONUS — unchanged const callBonus = readyToCallCount * 4; // 3. SCATTERED PAIR PENALTY — refined, context-aware // OLD: fires when matchedPairCount>=2 && matchedClaimable===0 // NEW: only fires when matched pairs are NOT supported by number structure // A pair is "on-path" if its number appears in another matched or near-complete group // in the same hand. Off-path pairs are penalized, on-path pairs are not. const matchedPairCount = details.matched.filter(m=>m.groupType==='pair').length; const matchedClaimable = details.matched.filter(m=>m.groupType!=='pair'&&m.groupType!=='single').length; const matchedNumbers = new Set(details.matched.map(m=>m.number).filter(Boolean)); // Count pairs whose number does NOT appear anywhere else in matched groups // These are the truly disconnected pairs const disconnectedPairs = details.matched.filter(m => { if (m.groupType !== 'pair') return false; // A pair is connected if same number appears in another matched group (different position) const sameNumElsewhere = details.matched.filter(o => o !== m && o.number === m.number && o.groupType !== 'pair' ).length > 0; return !sameNumElsewhere; }).length; // Penalize only truly disconnected pairs when there's no claimable structure at all const scatteredPairPenalty = (disconnectedPairs >= 2 && matchedClaimable === 0) ? disconnectedPairs * 2 // softer: 2pts per disconnected pair (was 3 per all pairs) : 0; // 4. CONCEALED PENALTY — unchanged // 5. COMPOUND PENALTY — smoother curve // OLD: ≤1 → mustDraw*3, >1 → mustDraw*(1+mustDraw*0.25)*2.5 (big jump at 2) // NEW: gradual quadratic — each additional draw adds proportionally more // 0→0, 1→3, 2→8, 3→15, 4→24 (was 0→0, 1→3, 2→12, 3→21) const mustDrawTilesNeeded = details.missing .filter(m => m.isPairSingle) .reduce((sum, m) => sum + m.need, 0); const compoundPenalty = mustDrawTilesNeeded > 0 ? Math.round(mustDrawTilesNeeded * 2 + (mustDrawTilesNeeded - 1) * mustDrawTilesNeeded * 0.8) : 0; // Curve: 1→2, 2→8, 3→16, 4→27 — gradual, no cliff at 2 // 6. RIGIDITY PENALTY — narrowed to avoid double-counting pairSingleMult // OLD: fires on singleGroupCount >= 3, penalty = (count-2)*4 // NEW: fires only when singles are ALSO disconnected from the hand's number structure // Singles that are part of a run or near-sequence are not penalized here // (pairSingleMult already handles their difficulty in scoreGroup) const singleGroupCount = handDef.groups.filter(g=>g.groupType==='single').length; // Determine which singles in missing groups are isolated (not near any matched number) const isolatedSingles = details.missing.filter(m => { if (m.groupType !== 'single') return false; if (!m.number) return true; // non-number singles are inherently isolated // Single is connected if an adjacent number (±1 or ±2) appears in matched groups const nearbyMatched = details.matched.some(o => o.number != null && Math.abs(o.number - m.number) <= 2 ); return !nearbyMatched; }).length; // Rigidity penalty only for isolated singles beyond 1 const rigidityPenalty = isolatedSingles >= 2 ? (isolatedSingles - 1) * 3 // softer: 3pts per extra isolated single (was 4 per extra single) : 0; // 7. FINAL SCORE — formula unchanged, constants adjusted const finalScore = Math.max(0, fitScore - Math.round(penalty * 2.2) // penalty multiplier unchanged - compoundPenalty - rigidityPenalty - scatteredPairPenalty + jokerBonus + callBonus - concPenalty ); } What Changed — Bullet Points scoreGroup: pairSingleMult now differentiates: partial pair (holds=1) → 1.3, missing pair (holds=0) → 1.8, single → 1.4. Modified scoreGroup javascript function scoreGroup(g, suit, pool) { let holds = 0; // [tile counting logic unchanged] // [pool consumption unchanged] const effective = Math.min(holds, g.count); const stillNeeded = Math.max(0, g.count - effective); const canClaim = g.groupType !== 'single' && g.groupType !== 'pair'; // BASE DIFFICULTY: driven purely by mechanics // How many tiles are missing, and can they be obtained via discard? // // Claimable groups (pung/kong/quint): missing tiles can come from discards // → much lower difficulty per missing tile // Pairs and singles: must be drawn naturally from wall // → higher difficulty per missing tile // Jokers: can substitute in claimable groups only, not pairs/singles // → joker availability reduces difficulty of claimable groups further // Effective jokers available for this group (jokers cannot fill pairs/singles) const jokersAvailable = canClaim ? hand.jokers : 0; const effectiveNeed = Math.max(0, stillNeeded - jokersAvailable); // NOTE: jokers not consumed from pool here — they are a flexible asset // handled at hand level. effectiveNeed used only for difficulty weighting. // DIFFICULTY WEIGHT: mechanics-only, no tile-type bias // Claimable group: // → each missing tile is low difficulty (can call from discard) // → if joker covers it, difficulty near zero // Pair: // → 0 held: very high difficulty (need both from wall) // → 1 held: medium difficulty (need one from wall) // → 2 held: zero difficulty (complete) // Single: // → must draw from wall, but only 1 tile needed // → medium-high difficulty let difficultyPerTile; if (canClaim) { // Missing from a claimable group — can call from discard // 1 missing → ready to call → very low difficulty // 2+ missing → needs wall tiles first → moderate difficultyPerTile = stillNeeded === 1 ? 0.6 : 1.0; } else if (g.groupType === 'pair') { if (holds === 0) difficultyPerTile = 2.0; // need both from wall if (holds === 1) difficultyPerTile = 1.4; // need one from wall if (holds >= 2) difficultyPerTile = 0; // complete — no penalty } else { // single difficultyPerTile = 1.3; } // REMOVE: competition weight (COMPETITION_WEIGHT lookup removed entirely) // REMOVE: honor discount (0.7 factor removed) // REMOVE: tile-type-based weight adjustments // All tile types treated identically — only structure determines difficulty const penalty = effectiveNeed * difficultyPerTile; // Claim state logic [unchanged — readyToCall / readyWithJoker / pullMoreThenCall / mustDraw] // dragonNote logic [unchanged] return { effective, stillNeeded, penalty, canClaim, dragonNote, holds, groupIsClaimable: canClaim, difficultyPerTile, effectiveNeed }; } Modified scoreHand javascript function scoreHand(handDef, suitMap, hand) { // [pool, sort, loop structure unchanged] // [claiming state logic unchanged] // ── Per-group penalty (inside loop) ────────────────────────────── // Penalty now comes directly from scoreGroup's mechanics-only difficulty // No additional multipliers applied here for tile type or honor status // groupPenalty = r.penalty (just use what scoreGroup returns) penalty += r.penalty; // ── After loop ─────────────────────────────────────────────────── const fitScore = Math.round((matched / total) * 100); // 1. JOKER BONUS — gradient, contextual // Jokers only help claimable groups. Value scales with how many // claimable groups exist and how viable the hand already is. // Gradient: 3pts/joker at fit=0, 7pts/joker at fit=100 // No cliff effect. No hard threshold. const jokerViabilityScale = 3 + (fitScore / 100) * 4; const jokerBonus = hand.jokers * jokerViabilityScale; // 2. CALL BONUS — unchanged const callBonus = readyToCallCount * 4; // 3. SCATTERED PAIR PENALTY — refined, structural check only // Penalize only pairs that are disconnected from the hand's number structure. // "Connected" = the pair's number appears within ±2 of another matched group's number. // Non-number pairs (winds, dragons in pair position) treated as disconnected // unless the hand section is winds_dragons. const matchedClaimable = details.matched.filter( m => m.groupType !== 'pair' && m.groupType !== 'single' ).length; const disconnectedPairs = details.matched.filter(m => { if (m.groupType !== 'pair') return false; if (!m.number) { // Honor pair — only connected in winds_dragons hands return handDef.section !== 'winds_dragons'; } // Number pair — connected if adjacent number (±2) in any other matched group return !details.matched.some( o => o !== m && o.number != null && Math.abs(o.number - m.number) <= 2 ); }).length; // Only fire when there are multiple disconnected pairs AND no claimable structure const scatteredPairPenalty = (disconnectedPairs >= 2 && matchedClaimable === 0) ? disconnectedPairs * 2 : 0; // 4. CONCEALED PENALTY — unchanged // 5. COMPOUND PENALTY — smooth quadratic curve // Captures the compounding difficulty of needing multiple natural draws. // Curve: 0→0, 1→2, 2→6, 3→12, 4→20 const mustDrawTilesNeeded = details.missing .filter(m => m.isPairSingle) .reduce((sum, m) => sum + m.need, 0); const compoundPenalty = mustDrawTilesNeeded > 0 ? Math.round(mustDrawTilesNeeded * 1.5 + (mustDrawTilesNeeded - 1) * mustDrawTilesNeeded * 0.7) : 0; // 6. RIGIDITY PENALTY — isolated singles only, no double-counting // Fires only when missing singles are structurally disconnected: // no adjacent matched number within ±2, and not a wind/dragon hand. // Does NOT fire based on count of singles in handDef — only on isolation. const isolatedMissingSingles = details.missing.filter(m => { if (m.groupType !== 'single') return false; if (!m.number) return handDef.section !== 'winds_dragons'; return !details.matched.some( o => o.number != null && Math.abs(o.number - m.number) <= 2 ); }).length; const rigidityPenalty = isolatedMissingSingles >= 2 ? (isolatedMissingSingles - 1) * 3 : 0; // 7. FINAL SCORE // Penalty multiplier reduced from 2.2 to 1.8 to compensate for // removal of competition weights (which previously inflated raw penalty). // Net effect: total penalty impact roughly preserved. const finalScore = Math.max(0, fitScore - Math.round(penalty * 1.8) - compoundPenalty - rigidityPenalty - scatteredPairPenalty + jokerBonus + callBonus - concPenalty ); return { fitScore, finalScore, penalty: Math.round(penalty * 10) / 10, matched, total, details, concPenalty, suitMap, jokerBonus, readyToCallCount, buildThenCallCount }; } What Changed — Bullet Points scoreGroup — Refinements smooth the curves and remove tile-type bias without flipping any of the 5 test results. The structural improvements (pair differentiation, isolation-based rigidity) will show more impact on real gameplay hands where mixed structure matters. One clarification: 1. Jokers should remain flexible and should not be explicitly assigned to a specific group during scoring. That reflects real gameplay better. Keep jokers as a flexible asset that improves claimable-group viability overall, rather than locking them into one group. 2. Single-heavy hands should still carry a real difficulty penalty. Singles are harder because they cannot be called from a discard before the hand is complete, and jokers cannot be used for them. 3. However, not all singles should be penalized equally. If singles are clearly supported by the hand structure, such as part of a consecutive run or aligned number pattern, their penalty can be softened. If singles are isolated, exact, or disconnected, their penalty should remain meaningfully higher. Please preserve this distinction in the scoring logic. Do not apply changes yet. Modified scoreGroup javascript function scoreGroup(g, suit, pool) { // [tile counting unchanged] // [pool consumption unchanged] const effective = Math.min(holds, g.count); const stillNeeded = Math.max(0, g.count - effective); const canClaim = g.groupType !== 'single' && g.groupType !== 'pair'; // DIFFICULTY: mechanics-only, no tile-type bias // Jokers remain a flexible hand-level asset — not assigned to specific groups here. // difficultyPerTile reflects only: // - whether the group can be claimed from a discard // - how many tiles are missing // - whether jokers CAN help (claimable) or CANNOT (pairs/singles) let difficultyPerTile; } else if (g.groupType === 'pair') { // Pairs: no calling, no jokers — must draw from wall // Differentiate by how many tiles are already held if (holds === 0) difficultyPerTile = 2.0; // need both from wall else if (holds === 1) difficultyPerTile = 1.4; // need one from wall else difficultyPerTile = 0; // complete } else { // Single: no calling before Mahjong, no jokers // Difficulty set at hand level based on structural context (see scoreHand) // Base value used here; adjusted externally per principle 3 difficultyPerTile = 1.3; } // REMOVE: COMPETITION_WEIGHT lookup // REMOVE: honor discount (0.7) // REMOVE: pairSingleMult flat multiplier // All tile types treated identically — structure determines difficulty only const penalty = stillNeeded * difficultyPerTile; // [dragonNote logic unchanged] // [canClaim / groupIsClaimable unchanged] return { effective, stillNeeded, penalty, canClaim, dragonNote, holds, groupIsClaimable: canClaim }; } Modified scoreHand javascript function scoreHand(handDef, suitMap, hand) { // [pool, sort, loop structure unchanged] // [claiming state logic unchanged] // ── Per-group penalty (inside loop) ────────────────────────────── // Use scoreGroup's mechanics-based penalty directly. // For SINGLE groups specifically, apply a structural context multiplier // based on whether the single is connected to the hand's number pattern. // This replaces the flat pairSingleMult and tile-type weighting. let groupPenalty = r.penalty; Reset bug — root cause and fix Root cause: resetApp() only cleared selectedTiles and switched screens. It did not touch the DOM. resultsContent kept all its child nodes — the old section focus, rec cards, discard card, pivot cards — in the DOM. When a new analysis ran, top3Container.innerHTML = '' cleared the rec cards but the results strip (added by prepend()) was never removed, so a second strip accumulated on top. Over multiple resets, results stacked. Fix: resetApp() now explicitly rebuilds resultsContent innerHTML with empty placeholder divs, clearing every rendered result node. Additionally, renderResults now removes any existing .results-hand-strip before prepending a new one, so duplicate strips can never accumulate even if reset logic changes in future. 4. Icon not updating — root cause and fix Root cause: Browsers and iOS aggressively cache PWA manifest files and icon assets. Even after replacing icon-192.png on the server, the browser served the cached version because the URL was identical. iOS additionally caches the apple-touch-icon independently of the manifest. Fix: Added ?v=2 query string to all icon references in both manifest.json and the tags in index.html. The browser treats these as new URLs, fetches fresh copies, and the new logo appears. The manifest link itself also gets ?v=2 to force the manifest to reload. To fully clear on iPhone: After deploying, delete the app from your home screen and re-add it. iOS does not update existing PWA icons in place — it must be re-installed once. Why this matters: This hand is more flexible than it may appear. If the user has two different numbers in the same suit plus corresponding opposing dragons, this hand should score as a meaningful possibility, even when the numbers seem far apart numerically (for example 2s and 9s in one suit). Numeric distance should not matter much here. What matters is: 1. same suit 2. exactly two distinct ranks with potential quint buildup 3. matching opposing dragon relationship What I need: 1. It’s just “two ranks in one suit.” The app needs to think like a mahjong player, not like a math teacher judging number relationships. Best way to encode it in the logic The strongest approach is this: For this hand only, have the evaluator: * look at each suit separately * find all distinct ranks present in that suit * build all possible 2-rank combinations from that suit * for each pair, score how well the rack fits: * count of rank A * count of rank B * count of correct opposing dragon * jokers * keep the best-scoring pair as the candidate for that hand That way, if the player has: * 2 bam x2 * 9 bam x3 * red dragons x2 * joker x1 the app sees: “Ah, this could be 22222 99999 DDDD,” instead of shrugging and wandering off to flirt with the wrong hand.
